data-social-tool="print">print</a></li></ul><p>New <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/kc/kansas-city-chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a> running back <a href="https://www.espn.com/nfl/player/_/id/15825/le'veon-bell">Le'Veon Bell</a> will have a $1 million base salary along with up to $1 million in playing time and playoff incentives, a source told ESPN's Jeremy Fowler.</p><p>The base salary will be prorated for the five games Bell was not on the Chiefs, meaning he will make around $690,000. He can earn up to $1.69 million in total this season with Kansas City before hitting 2021 free agency at age 29.</p><p>Bell signed with the Chiefs on Thursday, two days after he was released by the <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/nyj/new-york-jets">New York Jets</a>, ending a 19-month tenure that was filled with disappointment.</p><aside class="inline editorial float-r" data-behavior="article_related"><h1>Editor's Picks</h1><ul><li><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="img-link"><img src="https://a.espncdn.com/combiner/i?img=/photo/2020/0426/r692897_1296x1296_1-1.jpg&w=130&h=130&scale=crop&location=center"></a><h2><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="">RB Bell signs with defending champion Chiefs</a></h2></li></ul></aside><p>Bell, a three-time Pro Bowl selection, was a disappointment since signing a four-year, $52.5 million contract last year with the Jets, averaging only 3.3 yards per carry -- 51st out of 53 qualifying runners in the NFL during that span.</p><p>The Jets are responsible for the remaining $6 million on Bell's 2020 base pay, but there is an offset clause that will defray it by the amount of the salary on his new contract with the Chiefs.</p>

					mobile: 'init',
					tablet: 'init'
				};

				espnAdsConfig.load = espnAdsConfig.load || {};
				espnAdsConfig.load.defaults = liteAdLoadConfigs
				espnAdsConfig.load.frontpage = liteAdLoadConfigs;
				espnAdsConfig.load.index = liteAdLoadConfigs;
				espnAdsConfig.load.story = liteAdLoadConfigs;
			} else {
				espn.ads.loadGPT();
			}

			if (espnAdsConfig.prebidAdConfig && espnAdsConfig.prebidAdConfig.usePrebidBids) {
				

				// Load prebid.js for AppNexus
				(function() {
					var d = document, pbs = d.createElement('script'), pro = d.location.protocol;
					pbs.type = 'text/javascript';
					pbs.src = ((pro === 'https:') ? 'https' : 'http') + '://a.espncdn.com/prod/scripts/prebid3.17.0.js';
					var target = document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
					target.insertBefore(pbs, target.firstChild);
				})();
			}

			espn.ads.configPre = JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(espnAdsConfig));
		})();
	</script>

data-social-tool="print">print</a></li></ul><p>New <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/kc/kansas-city-chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a> running back <a href="https://www.espn.com/nfl/player/_/id/15825/le'veon-bell">Le'Veon Bell</a> will have a $1 million base salary along with up to $1 million in playing time and playoff incentives, a source told ESPN's Jeremy Fowler.</p><p>The base salary will be prorated for the five games Bell was not on the Chiefs, meaning he will make around $690,000. He can earn up to $1.69 million in total this season with Kansas City before hitting 2021 free agency at age 29.</p><p>Bell signed with the Chiefs on Thursday, two days after he was released by the <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/nyj/new-york-jets">New York Jets</a>, ending a 19-month tenure that was filled with disappointment.</p><aside class="inline editorial float-r" data-behavior="article_related"><h1>Editor's Picks</h1><ul><li><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="img-link"><img src="https://a.espncdn.com/combiner/i?img=/photo/2020/0426/r692897_1296x1296_1-1.jpg&w=130&h=130&scale=crop&location=center"></a><h2><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="">RB Bell signs with defending champion Chiefs</a></h2></li></ul></aside><p>Bell, a three-time Pro Bowl selection, was a disappointment since signing a four-year, $52.5 million contract last year with the Jets, averaging only 3.3 yards per carry -- 51st out of 53 qualifying runners in the NFL during that span.</p><p>The Jets are responsible for the remaining $6 million on Bell's 2020 base pay, but there is an offset clause that will defray it by the amount of the salary on his new contract with the Chiefs.</p>

data-social-tool="print">print</a></li></ul><p>New <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/kc/kansas-city-chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a> running back <a href="https://www.espn.com/nfl/player/_/id/15825/le'veon-bell">Le'Veon Bell</a> will have a $1 million base salary along with up to $1 million in playing time and playoff incentives, a source told ESPN's Jeremy Fowler.</p><p>The base salary will be prorated for the five games Bell was not on the Chiefs, meaning he will make around $690,000. He can earn up to $1.69 million in total this season with Kansas City before hitting 2021 free agency at age 29.</p><p>Bell signed with the Chiefs on Thursday, two days after he was released by the <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/nyj/new-york-jets">New York Jets</a>, ending a 19-month tenure that was filled with disappointment.</p><aside class="inline editorial float-r" data-behavior="article_related"><h1>Editor's Picks</h1><ul><li><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="img-link"><img src="https://a.espncdn.com/combiner/i?img=/photo/2020/0426/r692897_1296x1296_1-1.jpg&w=130&h=130&scale=crop&location=center"></a><h2><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="">RB Bell signs with defending champion Chiefs</a></h2></li></ul></aside><p>Bell, a three-time Pro Bowl selection, was a disappointment since signing a four-year, $52.5 million contract last year with the Jets, averaging only 3.3 yards per carry -- 51st out of 53 qualifying runners in the NFL during that span.</p><p>The Jets are responsible for the remaining $6 million on Bell's 2020 base pay, but there is an offset clause that will defray it by the amount of the salary on his new contract with the Chiefs.</p>

data-social-tool="print">print</a></li></ul><p>New <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/kc/kansas-city-chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a> running back <a href="https://www.espn.com/nfl/player/_/id/15825/le'veon-bell">Le'Veon Bell</a> will have a $1 million base salary along with up to $1 million in playing time and playoff incentives, a source told ESPN's Jeremy Fowler.</p><p>The base salary will be prorated for the five games Bell was not on the Chiefs, meaning he will make around $690,000. He can earn up to $1.69 million in total this season with Kansas City before hitting 2021 free agency at age 29.</p><p>Bell signed with the Chiefs on Thursday, two days after he was released by the <a href="/nfl/team/_/name/nyj/new-york-jets">New York Jets</a>, ending a 19-month tenure that was filled with disappointment.</p><aside class="inline editorial float-r" data-behavior="article_related"><h1>Editor's Picks</h1><ul><li><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="img-link"><img src="https://a.espncdn.com/combiner/i?img=/photo/2020/0426/r692897_1296x1296_1-1.jpg&w=130&h=130&scale=crop&location=center"></a><h2><a name="&lpos=story:editorspicks:inline:1" href="/nfl/story/_/id/30120515/rb-leveon-bell-expected-sign-kansas-city-chiefs" class="">RB Bell signs with defending champion Chiefs</a></h2></li></ul></aside><p>Bell, a three-time Pro Bowl selection, was a disappointment since signing a four-year, $52.5 million contract last year with the Jets, averaging only 3.3 yards per carry -- 51st out of 53 qualifying runners in the NFL during that span.</p><p>The Jets are responsible for the remaining $6 million on Bell's 2020 base pay, but there is an offset clause that will defray it by the amount of the salary on his new contract with the Chiefs.</p>
